<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Judd Trump</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Judd Trump</b> (born 20 August 1989)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-groveleisurejuddtrump_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-groveleisurejuddtrump-3">[3]</a></sup> is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a> player from <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and former world number one. He enjoyed considerable success in youth tournaments before turning professional in 2005. On 3 April 2011, Trump won his first <a href="/wiki/Snooker_world_rankings" title="Snooker world rankings">ranking</a> title, beating <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a> 10–8 in the final of the <a href="/wiki/2011_China_Open_(snooker)" title="2011 China Open (snooker)">China Open</a>. Following this success in China, he reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2011 World Snooker Championship">2011 World Snooker Championship</a> where he was defeated by <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a>. He then went on to win the <a href="/wiki/2011_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2011 UK Championship (snooker)">2011 UK Championship</a> where he defeated <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a> 10–8 in the final.</p>
<p>In November 2012, Trump won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2012_International_Championship" title="2012 International Championship">International Championship</a> and in doing so became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_world_number_one_snooker_players" title="List of world number one snooker players">world number one</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> a position he held for five weeks. On 18 February 2013, he reclaimed the top spot. In July 2014, Trump won his 4th ranking title at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Australian_Goldfields_Open" title="2014 Australian Goldfields Open">Australian Goldfields Open</a> after defeating <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> 9–5. He won the 2015 inaugural World Grand Prix beating Ronnie O'Sullivan 10–7 in the final. In October 2016, he again defeated Ronnie O'Sullivan 9-8 to claim the European Masters title.</p>
<p>Trump practises alongside <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lisowski" title="Jack Lisowski">Jack Lisowski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liang_Wenbo" title="Liang Wenbo">Liang Wenbo</a> at the Grove Snooker Academy in <a href="/wiki/Romford" title="Romford">Romford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>. A prolific break-builder, Trump has compiled more than 400 century breaks during his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> He is currently ranked at no. 4<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Amateur_career">Amateur career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Amateur career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Trump was English Under-13 and Under-15 champion, and reached the World Under-21 Championship semi-finals at the age of 14. At the same age, he became the youngest player ever to make a competitive 147, beating <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Jones_(snooker_player)" title="Jamie Jones (snooker player)">Jamie Jones</a>'s record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Professional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_season_2005/2006" title="Snooker season 2005/2006">2005/06</a> season he joined the professional tour, and at the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Open_(snooker)" title="Welsh Open (snooker)">Welsh Open</a> became the youngest player ever to qualify for the final stages of a ranking tournament. He reached the same last-48 stage for the China Open, losing 4–5 to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Holt_(snooker_player)" title="Michael Holt (snooker player)">Michael Holt</a>, although this was designated the final qualifying round and was actually played in <a href="/wiki/Prestatyn" title="Prestatyn">Prestatyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trump became the third youngest player at the time ever to reach the World Championship, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Snooker_Championship_2007" title="World Snooker Championship 2007">the 2007 event</a>, by beating <a href="/wiki/James_Wattana" title="James Wattana">James Wattana</a> 10–5, (with champions <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hendry" title="Stephen Hendry">Stephen Hendry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> respectively younger), and also with China's <a href="/wiki/Liu_Chuang_(snooker_player)" title="Liu Chuang (snooker player)">Liu Chuang</a> and Belgium's <a href="/wiki/Luca_Brecel" title="Luca Brecel">Luca Brecel</a> is one of only five 17-year-olds to feature at Sheffield's Crucible Theatre. Trump played the 2005 champion and 6th seed, <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Murphy_(snooker_player)" title="Shaun Murphy (snooker player)">Shaun Murphy</a>, in the first round, losing 6–10 despite having led 6–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trump did not build on this form in the 2007/08 season, only reaching the last 32 of the Welsh Open by beating <a href="/wiki/Joe_Swail" title="Joe Swail">Joe Swail</a>. He missed out on the <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2008 World Snooker Championship">World Championship</a> after a 9–10 loss to Swail, despite having led 9–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Things changed for the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_season_2008/2009" title="Snooker season 2008/2009">2008/09 season</a> when Trump reached the venue stages of the first four events. At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_(snooker)" title="Grand Prix (snooker)">Grand Prix</a> he benefited from <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Dott" title="Graeme Dott">Graeme Dott</a>'s withdrawal before defeating <a href="/wiki/Joe_Perry_(snooker_player)" title="Joe Perry (snooker player)">Joe Perry</a> 5–2 in the last 16, despite admitting to not playing well and Perry feeling that he had outplayed Trump.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Then came the biggest win of his career so far, defeating Ronnie O'Sullivan 5–4 to reach the semi-final, in which he was defeated 6–4 by <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a>. He beat double world champion <a href="/wiki/Mark_Williams_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Williams (snooker player)">Mark Williams</a> to qualify for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahrain_Championship_2008" title="Bahrain Championship 2008">2008 Bahrain Championship</a>. He won a qualifying tournament to gain entry into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Masters_Snooker" title="2009 Masters Snooker">2009 Masters Tournament</a> as the only qualifier, but was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a> in the first round. He failed to qualify for the World Championship, losing 8–10 to <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Lee" title="Stephen Lee">Stephen Lee</a> having led 6–3. Lee considered this match to be a local derby, as he is from nearby <a href="/wiki/Trowbridge" title="Trowbridge">Trowbridge</a>. He also noted that Trump had not followed the custom of apologising for fluked shots during the match, and concluded "all I've heard about for the last five years is how good he is. Today he blew a 6–3 lead and hopefully that will stick with him".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Trump ended the season in the Top 32 of the rankings for the first time. He was coached for a short time by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Chappel" title="Tony Chappel">Tony Chappel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trump also qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2009_Premier_League_Snooker" title="2009 Premier League Snooker">2009 Premier League</a>, by winning the <a href="/wiki/2009_Championship_League" title="2009 Championship League">2009 Championship League</a>. In the event he won four of his six matches, including a 4–2 win over <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> and finished second in the League table. However, he lost 1–5 to O'Sullivan in his semi-final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_season_2009/2010" title="Snooker season 2009/2010">2009/2010</a> season in ranking events was less successful for Trump as he failed to progress beyond the last 32 in any of the tournaments. In January 2010, Trump joined Romford-based snooker agency Grove Leisure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.2F2011">2010/2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2010/2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_season_2010/2011" title="Snooker season 2010/2011">2010/2011</a> season, he reached his first professional ranking event final at the <a href="/wiki/2011_China_Open_(snooker)" title="2011 China Open (snooker)">2011 China Open</a>. He defeated former Masters champion <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a> 10–8 to win his first major title,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and provisionally climb into the top 16 of the world rankings. On his way to winning the China Open final, Trump made his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_snooker_players_with_over_100_century_breaks" title="List of snooker players with over 100 century breaks">100th competitive century break</a>.</p>
<p>Trump had already qualified for the World Championship when he won the China Open, and was drawn against reigning champion <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> in the first round, whom he defeated 10–8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In subsequent rounds, he knocked out <a href="/wiki/Martin_Gould" title="Martin Gould">Martin Gould</a> 13–6, <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Dott" title="Graeme Dott">Graeme Dott</a> 13–5 and <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a> 17–15 to qualify for his first World Championship final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In the final Trump lost 15–18 to <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.2F2012">2011/2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2011/2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Judd started the season with a 3–5 loss to <a href="/wiki/Mark_Davis_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Davis (snooker player)">Mark Davis</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Australian_Goldfields_Open" title="2011 Australian Goldfields Open">2011 Australian Goldfields Open</a> first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> However, this disappointment was soon forgotten as he won the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2011/2012_%E2%80%93_Event_2" title="Players Tour Championship 2011/2012 – Event 2">2nd PTC</a> of the Season, beating <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a> 4–0 in the final at a virtual home venue of the South West Snooker Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Judd then lost 5–1 against <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bingham" title="Stuart Bingham">Stuart Bingham</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Shanghai_Masters" title="2011 Shanghai Masters">Shanghai Masters</a> first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Trump finished runner-up to <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2011/2012_%E2%80%93_Event_8" title="Players Tour Championship 2011/2012 – Event 8">8th PTC event</a> of the season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> but immediately rediscovered his winning touch by capturing <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2011/2012_%E2%80%93_Event_9" title="Players Tour Championship 2011/2012 – Event 9">Event 9</a> by defeating <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> 4–3 in the final in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, Belgium in just over an hours worth of play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> He would later top the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2011/2012#Order_of_Merit" title="Players Tour Championship 2011/2012">Order of Merit</a> after all twelve PTC events had been played, thus qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2011/2012_%E2%80%93_Finals" title="Players Tour Championship 2011/2012 – Finals">2012 Finals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> He suffered a shock in the last 16 as world number 51 <a href="/wiki/Xiao_Guodong" title="Xiao Guodong">Xiao Guodong</a> beat him 2–4, despite playing with a broken bone in his hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 December 2011, Trump won his second ranking event tournament, the <a href="/wiki/2011_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2011 UK Championship (snooker)">2011 UK Championship</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Barbican_Centre,_York" title="Barbican Centre, York">Barbican Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>. Trump beat <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Dale" title="Dominic Dale">Dominic Dale</a> 6–4 in the last 32, before winning the final two frames of the second round to edge out <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a>, 6–5. After the match Trump claimed that he had been "outplayed" and was "lucky" to have got through.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> He then dispatched <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Maguire" title="Stephen Maguire">Stephen Maguire</a> 6–3<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and faced <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> in the semi-finals. The semi-final was a tight and nervy affair, with Trump stating afterwards that he believed Robertson was trying to stifle his natural game by, "slowing it down" and "making things awkward", but nevertheless the <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristolian</a> triumphed, 9–7 to reach his first UK final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In the final he played <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a> and trailed 1–3 early on in the best-of-19 frames match. However, Trump then produced a match-defining run of seven straight frames to take an 8–3 lead. Despite a strong fightback from Allen, who won five of the next six frames to trail just 8–9, Trump went on to clinch the 18th frame with a break of 91 and win the final by 10 frames to 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Six-time winner of the event, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Davis" title="Steve Davis">Steve Davis</a>, said that Trump's performances during the championship had shown that he was "spearheading his generation" of snooker players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The victory took him up to a career-high world ranking of 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>He continued his fine form by reaching the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Masters_(snooker)" title="2012 Masters (snooker)">Masters</a> in January. He beat <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bingham" title="Stuart Bingham">Stuart Bingham</a> in the first round and O'Sullivan once more in the quarters 6–2, to make his record against the four-time World Champion five wins and two defeats, from their seven meetings in tournament play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> He played Robertson in the last four for the second successive major event and it was the Australian who exacted his revenge from the defeat suffered in York a month earlier, as he triumphed 6–3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> He reached three quarter-finals in his next four ranking events to become the world number 2 in April, behind <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a>, meaning Trump had risen seven places in the rankings this season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2012 World Snooker Championship">2012 World Championship</a>, he beat Dominic Dale in his first round match by a 10–7 scoreline, despite suffering from food poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> However, he was knocked out by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allister_Carter" title="Allister Carter">Ali Carter</a> 12–13 in the second round having let a 12–9 lead slip, ending his chances to become world number 1 this season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.2F2013">2012/2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2012/2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Trump started the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_season_2012/2013" title="Snooker season 2012/2013">season</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Wuxi_Classic" title="2012 Wuxi Classic">Wuxi Classic</a> in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, where he lost to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Milkins" title="Robert Milkins">Robert Milkins</a> 3–5 in the second round, having beaten <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Dale" title="Dominic Dale">Dominic Dale</a> 5–1 in the opener.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13-38">[38]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2012_Shanghai_Masters" title="2012 Shanghai Masters">Shanghai Masters</a> he saw off <a href="/wiki/Barry_Hawkins" title="Barry Hawkins">Barry Hawkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Dott" title="Graeme Dott">Graeme Dott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Williams_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Williams (snooker player)">Mark Williams</a> to reach the final where he faced <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13-38">[38]</a></sup> Trump surged into a 5–0 lead and, despite Higgins making a 147 break in the next frame, claimed a 7–2 advantage after the first session. Upon the resumption of play Higgins won six frames in a row with the match eventually going into a deciding frame. Trump made a break of 35, but ran out of position and Higgins was able to secure the title with a 10–9 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> However, Trump was able to bounce back at the next ranking event, the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2012_International_Championship" title="2012 International Championship">International Championship</a>, by claiming his third ranking event title. He eliminated <a href="/wiki/Fergal_O%27Brien" title="Fergal O'Brien">Fergal O'Brien</a> 6–3, <a href="/wiki/Aditya_Mehta" title="Aditya Mehta">Aditya Mehta</a> 6–0 and then edged past Allen 6–5 in the quarter-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Trump thrashed <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ebdon" title="Peter Ebdon">Peter Ebdon</a> 9–1 in the semi-finals to become snooker's tenth world number one,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and recovered from 6–8 down in the final against <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> to triumph 10–8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_(DerHexer)_2013-01-30_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2271" data-file-width="3346" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg/220px-Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg/330px-Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg/440px-Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_%28DerHexer%29_2013-01-30_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Judd_Trump_at_Snooker_German_Masters_(DerHexer)_2013-01-30_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Judd Trump at <a href="/wiki/2013_German_Masters" title="2013 German Masters">2013 German Masters</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Trump met <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a> in back to back <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2012/2013" title="Players Tour Championship 2012/2013">Players Tour Championship</a> finals, losing the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2012/2013_%E2%80%93_Event_4" title="Players Tour Championship 2012/2013 – Event 4">first</a> 2–4, but gained revenge in the second, the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour_2012/2013_%E2%80%93_Event_4" title="European Tour 2012/2013 – Event 4">Bulgarian Open</a> by whitewashing him 4–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13-38">[38]</a></sup> Trump reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Premier_League_Snooker" title="2012 Premier League Snooker">Premier League</a> having beating <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> in the semi-finals, but lost 2–7 to <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bingham" title="Stuart Bingham">Stuart Bingham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In the defence of his 2011 <a href="/wiki/2012_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2012 UK Championship (snooker)">UK Championship</a> title, Trump played <a href="/wiki/Mark_Joyce" title="Mark Joyce">Mark Joyce</a> in the first round. Despite leading 3–0 and 5–2, Trump lost the last four frames of the match to suffer a major shock exit against the world number 50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The disappointment was compounded when <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a> went on to win the title, reclaiming the top ranking in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Trump was defeated 1–6 by <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Dott" title="Graeme Dott">Graeme Dott</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Masters_(snooker)" title="2013 Masters (snooker)">Masters</a> and 4–5 by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Hamilton_(snooker_player)" title="Anthony Hamilton (snooker player)">Anthony Hamilton</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2013_German_Masters" title="2013 German Masters">German Masters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13-38">[38]</a></sup> He regained his form and the world number one ranking at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Welsh_Open_(snooker)" title="2013 Welsh Open (snooker)">Welsh Open</a>. He came back from 1–3 down to beat <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Dale" title="Dominic Dale">Dominic Dale</a> 4–3 in the first round, after which he asserted that "players are changing their game to play slower against me. Dominic was too slow for himself and it caught him out towards the end".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> More comfortable victories ensued over <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Higginson" title="Andrew Higginson">Andrew Higginson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pankaj_Advani" title="Pankaj Advani">Pankaj Advani</a> to set up a semi-final meeting with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Maguire" title="Stephen Maguire">Stephen Maguire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13-38">[38]</a></sup> Trump initially raced into a 2–0 lead only to lose five frames in succession to the rejuvenated Maguire. Trump pulled back two more frames and looked set to force a decider after a 50 break in the tenth frame, but Maguire ground out the frame and won 6–4. After the match Trump reiterated that titles take precedence over world ranking: “I take no consolation tonight from getting back to world number one. I want to win tournaments and titles, that is why I am here".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Open_(snooker)" title="2013 World Open (snooker)">World Open</a> he gained revenge over Joyce by dispatching him 5–0 and beat <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Bond" title="Nigel Bond">Nigel Bond</a> 5–1, before <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Stevens" title="Matthew Stevens">Matthew Stevens</a> won their last eight match 5–3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Trump qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2012/2013_%E2%80%93_Finals" title="Players Tour Championship 2012/2013 – Finals">PTC Finals</a> by finishing second on the Order of Merit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> but lost to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_Burden" title="Alfred Burden">Alfie Burden</a> 3–4 in the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He also lost in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2013_China_Open_(snooker)" title="2013 China Open (snooker)">China Open</a> 3–5 to good friend <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lisowski" title="Jack Lisowski">Jack Lisowski</a>, surrendering his world number one ranking to <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a> in the process and headed into the <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2013 World Snooker Championship">World Championship</a> in less than auspicious form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trump said that he had prepared better than ever for the World Championship and beat <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Dale" title="Dominic Dale">Dominic Dale</a> in the first round for the second year in a row, this time by 10–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> At 8–7 ahead in the last 16 against <a href="/wiki/Marco_Fu" title="Marco Fu">Marco Fu</a>, Trump raced away with five consecutive frames to triumph 13–7 and set up a quarter-final clash with <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Murphy_(snooker_player)" title="Shaun Murphy (snooker player)">Shaun Murphy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Trump came from 3–8 down to level at 8–8 at the conclusion of the second session. The deciding frame lasted 53 minutes with Trump winning it on the yellow to seal a 13–12 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> He played against <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> in the semi-finals, but was unable to capitalise on the chances that came his way: though he potted a ball in 24 of the 28 frames played, he could only make four breaks above 50 in an 11–17 defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Trump said afterwards "It's probably the worst I've played all tournament. I would've probably expected to lose to anyone the way I played."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.2F2014">2013/2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2013/2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the start of the season Trump was ranked third in the <a href="/wiki/Snooker_world_rankings_2013/2014" title="Snooker world rankings 2013/2014">world rankings</a>. He began the season poorly as he lost in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Wuxi_Classic" title="2013 Wuxi Classic">Wuxi Classic</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Shanghai_Masters" title="2013 Shanghai Masters">Shanghai Masters</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_International_Championship" title="2013 International Championship">International Championship</a>, as well as failing to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Indian_Open" title="2013 Indian Open">Indian Open</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013.2F14_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-2013.2F14-58">[58]</a></sup> In November, he reached the final of the minor-ranking <a href="/wiki/European_Tour_2013/2014_%E2%80%93_Event_6" title="European Tour 2013/2014 – Event 6">Kay Suzanne Memorial Cup</a> but lost 4–1 to <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Later in the month, he made the first official <a href="/wiki/Maximum_break" title="Maximum break">maximum break</a> of his career in the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour_2013/2014_%E2%80%93_Event_7" title="European Tour 2013/2014 – Event 7">Antwerp Open</a> during a last 32 defeat against <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> He reached the fourth round of the <a href="/wiki/2013_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2013 UK Championship (snooker)">UK Championship</a> where Allen defeated him 6–4 and lost 6–5 to <a href="/wiki/Marco_Fu" title="Marco Fu">Marco Fu</a> in the opening round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Masters_(snooker)" title="2014 Masters (snooker)">Masters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013.2F14_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-2013.2F14-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2014_German_Masters" title="2014 German Masters">German Masters</a> he dropped just four frames in winning five matches to reach his first ranking final of the season where he played <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a>. Trump was two frames ahead twice in the first session but ended it level at 4–4 and he lost five of the next six frames upon the resumption of play to be defeated 9–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Welsh_Open_(snooker)" title="2014 Welsh Open (snooker)">Welsh Open</a>, he was beaten 4–3 by <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a> in the last 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Higgins was again the victor when the two met in the last 16 of the <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Open_(snooker)" title="2014 World Open (snooker)">World Open</a> winning 5–4 after Trump had taken a 4–0 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Trump won the non-ranking <a href="/wiki/2014_Championship_League" title="2014 Championship League">Championship League</a> title during the season by beating <a href="/wiki/Martin_Gould" title="Martin Gould">Martin Gould</a> 3–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2014 World Snooker Championship">World Championship</a>, Trump defeated <a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford_(snooker_player)" title="Tom Ford (snooker player)">Tom Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Day" title="Ryan Day">Ryan Day</a> to reach the quarter-finals, where he played <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013.2F14_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-2013.2F14-58">[58]</a></sup> Trump led 6–2, 9–6, and 11–8 before Robertson mounted a determined fightback to take the last five frames and win the match 13–11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Trump received criticism for not acknowledging Robertson becoming the first player to make 100 centuries in a single season during the match, instead choosing to walk out of the arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Trump said later that Robertson's feat meant nothing to him and he chose to congratulate his opponent after the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.2F2015">2014/2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2014/2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Trump was thrashed 5–0 by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Maguire" title="Stephen Maguire">Stephen Maguire</a> in the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wuxi_Classic" title="2014 Wuxi Classic">Wuxi Classic</a>, but responded a week later by claiming his fourth ranking title and first for 20 months at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Australian_Goldfields_Open" title="2014 Australian Goldfields Open">Australian Goldfields Open</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014.2F15_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014.2F15-70">[70]</a></sup> He beat home favourite <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> 9–5 in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Trump reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour_2014/2015_%E2%80%93_Event_2" title="European Tour 2014/2015 – Event 2">Paul Hunter Classic</a> but lost 4–2 to <a href="/wiki/Mark_Allen_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Allen (snooker player)">Mark Allen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> He then suffered first and second round exits to <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Dale" title="Dominic Dale">Dominic Dale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Burnett" title="Jamie Burnett">Jamie Burnett</a> respectively in the next two ranking events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014.2F15_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014.2F15-70">[70]</a></sup> Trump advanced to the final of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Champion_of_Champions" title="2014 Champion of Champions">Champion of Champions</a> and fell 8–3 down to <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a>, before reducing his deficit to a single frame in taking four successive frames with the help of two centuries. However, O'Sullivan would win the two frames he needed to triumph 10–7, with Trump claiming his opponent's standard throughout the match had been the best he has ever played against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The pair also met in the final of the <a href="/wiki/2014_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2014 UK Championship (snooker)">UK Championship</a> in which Trump was 9–4 behind with a high break of 56. However, he won the next frame and then made back-to-back centuries and an 86 to only trail 9–8. He was 59–0 down in the next, but cleared with a 67 to send the match into an unlikely decider which he lost when O'Sullivan made a title winning break after Trump had failed to escape from a snooker. O'Sullivan described the match as the hardest of his career afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Masters_(snooker)" title="2015 Masters (snooker)">Masters</a>, Trump lost 6–4 against <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Maguire" title="Stephen Maguire">Stephen Maguire</a> in the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Trump made the second 147 of his career in the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2015_German_Masters" title="2015 German Masters">German Masters</a>, but was knocked out 5–4 by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Grand_Prix" title="2015 World Grand Prix">World Grand Prix</a> Trump eliminated <a href="/wiki/Mark_Williams_(snooker_player)" title="Mark Williams (snooker player)">Mark Williams</a> 4–3 on the final black, but then fell 5–1 down to <a href="/wiki/Martin_Gould" title="Martin Gould">Martin Gould</a> in the semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> However, Trump then outscored Gould 395–37 to take five successive frames and beat him 6–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> He played O'Sullivan for the third time in a final this season and was 7–4 behind. Trump then won six frames in a row which included a 142 break, the highest of the tournament, to win 10–7 and claim his second title of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Trump reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/Players_Tour_Championship_2014/2015_%E2%80%93_Finals" title="Players Tour Championship 2014/2015 – Finals">PTC Grand Final</a>, where he lost 4–2 to Williams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014.2F15_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-2014.2F15-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trump produced his best snooker in the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2015 World Snooker Championship">World Championship</a> as he knocked in four centuries during a 13–4 thrashing of <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a> and stated that if he could play to the same standard in the rest of the event he would secure his first world title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> After holding an early 2–1 lead over <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bingham" title="Stuart Bingham">Stuart Bingham</a> in the semi-finals, Trump could not regain the lead and fell 16–14 behind. He then made successive centuries to force a deciding frame in which he missed a red to the middle pocket due to a kick and Bingham would go on to take the match 17–16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.2F2016">2015/2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2015/2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the defence of his <a href="/wiki/2015_Australian_Goldfields_Open" title="2015 Australian Goldfields Open">Australian Goldfields Open</a> title, Trump was knocked out in the quarter-finals 5–1 by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Maguire" title="Stephen Maguire">Stephen Maguire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015.2F16_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015.2F16-82">[82]</a></sup> He reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Shanghai_Masters" title="2015 Shanghai Masters">Shanghai Masters</a>, but a slow start from Trump saw him trail world number 54 <a href="/wiki/Kyren_Wilson" title="Kyren Wilson">Kyren Wilson</a> 6–3 after the first session. Wilson also had leads of 8–4 and 9–7, before Trump sent the match into a deciding frame which Wilson won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Trump scored 278 points to nil in taking the first three frames of his third round <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_UK_Championship_(snooker)" title="2015 UK Championship (snooker)">UK Championship</a> match with <a href="/wiki/Liang_Wenbo" title="Liang Wenbo">Liang Wenbo</a>, but went on to lose 6–4. Trump branded the collapse an embarrassment and said it was the worst he had felt as a professional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In the new year Trump and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Robertson_(snooker_player)" title="Neil Robertson (snooker player)">Neil Robertson</a> set a record of six centuries in a best-of-11 frame match (four from Trump and two from Robertson). Trump closed it out with a sublime 129 break to win 6–5, with Robertson describing it as the greatest match in Masters' history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> He was knocked out 6–4 in the semi-finals by <a href="/wiki/Barry_Hawkins" title="Barry Hawkins">Barry Hawkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first title of the season came at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Championship_League" title="2016 Championship League">Championship League</a> by defeating <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> 3–2 in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Soon afterwards he won his fifth ranking title and first for almost two years by beating <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Walden" title="Ricky Walden">Ricky Walden</a> 10–4 in the <a href="/wiki/2016_China_Open_(snooker)" title="2016 China Open (snooker)">China Open</a> final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> After trailing <a href="/wiki/Liang_Wenbo" title="Liang Wenbo">Liang Wenbo</a> 7–3 in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Snooker_Championship" title="2016 World Snooker Championship">World Championship</a>, Trump tweeted that the drinks would be on him if he could turn it around. He duly did by winning 10–8 and put a few hundred pounds behind the local bar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Trump could not escape from a similar position against <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a> in the second round and was beaten 13–10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016.2F2017">2016/2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2016/2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Trump thrashed <a href="/wiki/John_Higgins_(snooker_player)" title="John Higgins (snooker player)">John Higgins</a> 4–0 in the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2016_European_Masters" title="2016 European Masters">2016 European Masters</a> and then overcame <a href="/wiki/Mark_Selby" title="Mark Selby">Mark Selby</a> 6–2 to play <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_O%27Sullivan" title="Ronnie O'Sullivan">Ronnie O'Sullivan</a> in the final. Trump was down 8–6, but took each of the final three frames to triumph 9–8 and win his sixth ranking title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In his next event, the <a href="/wiki/2016_English_Open_(snooker)" title="2016 English Open (snooker)">English Open</a>, he comfortably beat Higgins in the quarter-finals again, this time 5–1 and then defeated <a href="/wiki/Barry_Hawkins" title="Barry Hawkins">Barry Hawkins</a> 6–2 to make it 14 wins in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Trump lost 9–6 to <a href="/wiki/Liang_Wenbo" title="Liang Wenbo">Liang Wenbo</a> in the final after having missed a good chance to make it 7–7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Trump edged past <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Murphy_(snooker_player)" title="Shaun Murphy (snooker player)">Shaun Murphy</a> 6–5 on the final black to reach the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2016_International_Championship" title="2016 International Championship">International Championship</a> and was knocked out 9–4 by <a href="/wiki/Ding_Junhui" title="Ding Junhui">Ding Junhui</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.2F17_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016.2F17-94">[94]</a></sup> He had a surprise 6–2 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Lines" title="Oliver Lines">Oliver Lines</a> in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2016_UK_Championship" title="2016 UK Championship">UK Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Trump was 5–1 up on Higgins in the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Scottish_Open_(snooker)" title="2016 Scottish Open (snooker)">Scottish Open</a> as he made three centuries and a 99 break, but Higgins recovered to win 6–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_and_rankings_timeline">Performance and rankings timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Judd_Trump&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Performance and rankings timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>

<th colspan="6">Performance Table Legend</th>

<tr>
<td align="center" style="color:#cccccc;" width="30">LQ</td>
<td>lost in the qualifying draw</td>
<td align="center" style="background:#afeeee;">#R</td>
<td>lost in the early rounds of the tournament<br/>
(WR = Wildcard round, RR = Round robin)</td>
<td align="center" style="background:#ffebcd;">QF</td>
<td>lost in the quarter-finals</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" style="background:yellow;">SF</td>
<td>lost in the semi-finals</td>
<td align="center" style="background:#D8BFD8;">F</td>
<td>lost in the final</td>
<td align="center" style="background:#00ff00;"><b>W</b></td>
<td>won the tournament</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" style="color:#cccccc;" width="30">DNQ</td>
<td>did not qualify for the tournament</td>
<td align="center" style="color:#cccccc;" width="30">A</td>
<td>did not participate in the tournament</td>
<td align="center" style="color:#cccccc;" width="30">WD</td>
<td>withdrew from the tournament</td>
</tr>
